## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, time t, and velocity v, which is the standard state-space form of a (possibly driven/damped) nonlinear oscillator. Typical structures combine restoring forces in x, damping terms in v, and optional external forcing terms in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring acceleration, sign absorbed in c0)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (small-velocity linear drag plus linear restoring force)
- Time-dependent stiffness (parametric excitation / Mathieu-type): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (parametric modulation of restoring term)
- Constant external force / bias: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 (gravity/offset or equilibrium shift)
- Sinusoidal driving force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (externally driven oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger nonlinear restoring force)
- Quadratic (asymmetric) stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (broken symmetry / asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear (quadratic/cubic) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (turbulent-like drag or nonlinear dissipation)
- Mixed nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (odd-power velocity damping for symmetric dissipation)
- Position-dependent damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (damping increases with displacement/strain)
- State-coupled nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent dissipation typical in nonlinear oscillators)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (and not on v or t), implying a potential-derived restoring force.
- Dissipation signature: dv_dt includes terms proportional to v or odd functions of v (e.g., v, v*Abs(v), v**3), indicating energy loss per cycle.
- Symmetric restoring force about x=0: restoring acceleration is an odd function of x (x, x**3, x**5); even powers (x**2) indicate asymmetry.
- Hardening vs softening spring: positive vs negative cubic stiffness term (c * x**3) changes frequency with amplitude (backbone curve behavior).
- External periodic driving: additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms produce steady-state oscillations and resonance phenomena.
- Parametric excitation: time-periodic coefficient multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) produces Mathieu-type instabilities and parametric resonance.
- Nonlinear drag regime change: inclusion of v*Abs(v) suggests drag scaling like speed squared (common at higher Reynolds number analogs).
- Amplitude-dependent damping: factors like (c0 + c1*x**2)*v or x**2*v indicate dissipation increases with oscillation amplitude.
